<ul><li><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="180" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/16px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/23px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/31px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png 2x" title="Category" width="16"/> <a href="/wiki/Category:Infrastructure" title="Category:Infrastructure">Category</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" decoding="async" height="28" title="Portal:Engineering">Engineering portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Public_Infrastructure" title="Template:Public Infrastructure"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Public_Infrastructure" title="Template talk:Public Infrastructure"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Public_Infrastructure&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A <b>hospital</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> institution providing <a href="/wiki/Patient" title="Patient">patient</a> treatment with specialized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Science" title="Medical Science">health science</a> and auxiliary healthcare staff and medical equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The best-known type of hospital is the general hospital, which typically has an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">emergency department</a> to treat urgent health problems ranging from fire and accident victims to a sudden illness. A district hospital typically is the major health care facility in its region, with many beds for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intensive_care" title="Intensive care">intensive care</a> and additional beds for patients who need long-term care. Specialized hospitals include <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">trauma centers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_hospital" title="Rehabilitation hospital">rehabilitation hospitals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_hospital" title="Children's hospital">children's hospitals</a>, seniors' (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geriatric" title="Geriatric">geriatric</a>) hospitals, and hospitals for dealing with specific medical needs such as <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">psychiatric</a> treatment (see <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric hospital</a>) and certain disease categories. Specialized hospitals can help reduce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_costs" title="Health care costs">health care costs</a> compared to general hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-3">[3]</a></sup> Hospitals are classified as general, specialty, or government depending on the sources of income received.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospital</a> combines assistance to people with teaching to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Science" title="Medical Science">health science</a> students  and <a href="/wiki/Allied_Healthcare" title="Allied Healthcare">auxiliary healthcare</a> students. A health science  facility smaller than a hospital is generally called a <a href="/wiki/Clinic" title="Clinic">clinic</a>. Hospitals have a range of departments (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">surgery</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urgent_care" title="Urgent care">urgent care</a>) and specialist units such as <a href="/wiki/Cardiology" title="Cardiology">cardiology</a>. Some hospitals have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outpatient" title="Outpatient">outpatient departments</a> and some have chronic treatment units. Common support units include a <a href="/wiki/Hospital_pharmacy" title="Hospital pharmacy">pharmacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pathology" title="Pathology">pathology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radiology" title="Radiology">radiology</a>.
</p><p>Hospitals are typically funded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publicly_funded_healthcare" title="Publicly funded healthcare">public funding</a>, health organisations (<a href="/wiki/For-profit_hospital" title="For-profit hospital">for-profit</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-profit_organisation" title="Non-profit organisation">nonprofit</a>), <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a> companies, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charitable_organisation" title="Charitable organisation">charities</a>, including direct charitable donations. Historically, hospitals were often founded and funded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_orders" title="Religious orders">religious orders</a>, or by charitable individuals and leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Currently, hospitals are largely staffed by professional <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeons</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Allied_health_professions" title="Allied health professions">allied health practitioners</a>, whereas in the past, this work was usually performed by the members of founding religious orders or by <a href="/wiki/Volunteering" title="Volunteering">volunteers</a>. However, there are various Catholic religious orders, such as the <a href="/wiki/Alexians" title="Alexians">Alexians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bon_Secours_Sisters" title="Bon Secours Sisters">Bon Secours Sisters</a> that still focus on hospital ministry in the late 1990s, as well as several other Christian denominations, including the Methodists and Lutherans, which run hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In accordance with the original meaning of the word, hospitals were original "places of hospitality", and this meaning is still preserved in the names of some institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hospital_Chelsea" title="Royal Hospital Chelsea">Royal Hospital Chelsea</a>, established in 1681 as a retirement and nursing home for veteran soldiers.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospital.svg"><img alt="White H on blue background, used to represent hospitals in the US." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hospital.svg/220px-Hospital.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hospital.svg/330px-Hospital.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hospital.svg/440px-Hospital.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospital.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During peacetime, hospitals can be indicated by a variety of symbols. For example, a white 'H' on a blue background is often used in the United States. During times of armed conflict, a hospital may be marked with the emblem of the <a href="/wiki/Emblems_of_the_International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="Emblems of the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">red cross, red crescent or red crystal</a> in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>During the Middle Ages, hospitals served different functions from modern institutions in that they were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almshouses" title="Almshouses">almshouses</a> for the poor, <a href="/wiki/Hostel" title="Hostel">hostels</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilgrims" title="Pilgrims">pilgrims</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Hospital_school" title="Hospital school">hospital schools</a>. The word "hospital" comes from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">hospes</i></span>, signifying a stranger or foreigner, hence a guest. Another noun derived from this, <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">hospitium</i></span> came to signify hospitality, that is the relation between guest and shelterer, hospitality, friendliness, and hospitable reception. By <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonymy</a>, the Latin word then came to mean a guest-chamber, guest's lodging, an <a href="/wiki/Inn" title="Inn">inn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Hospes</i></span> is thus the root for the English words <i>host</i> (where the <i>p</i> was dropped for convenience of pronunciation) <i><a href="/wiki/Hospitality" title="Hospitality">hospitality</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hospice" title="Hospice">hospice</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hostel" title="Hostel">hostel</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hotel" title="Hotel">hotel</a></i>. The latter modern word derives from Latin via the <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> romance word <span title="Old French (842-ca. 1400)-language text"><i lang="fro">hostel</i></span>, which developed a silent <i>s</i>, which letter was eventually removed from the word, the loss of which is signified by a <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">circumflex</a> in the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">modern French</a> word <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">hôtel</i></span>. The <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> word <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Spital</i></span> shares similar roots.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types"><span class="anchor" id="Types"></span>Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Patient" title="Patient">patients</a> go to a hospital just for <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis" title="Diagnosis">diagnosis</a>, treatment, or therapy and then leave ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outpatients" title="Outpatients">outpatients</a>") without staying overnight; while others are "admitted" and stay overnight or for several days or weeks or months ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inpatients" title="Inpatients">inpatients</a>"). Hospitals are usually distinguished from other types of medical facilities by their ability to admit and care for inpatients whilst the others, which are smaller, are often described as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinics" title="Clinics">clinics</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_and_acute_care">General and acute care<span class="anchor" id="General_hospital"></span><span class="anchor" id="General"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General and acute care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"General hospital" redirects here. For the American soap opera, see <a href="/wiki/General_Hospital" title="General Hospital">General Hospital</a>.</div>
<p>The best-known type of hospital is the general hospital, also known as an acute-care hospital. These facilities handle many kinds of disease and injury, and normally have an emergency department (sometimes known as "accident &amp; emergency") or <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">trauma center</a> to deal with immediate and urgent threats to health. Larger cities may have several hospitals of varying sizes and facilities. Some hospitals, especially in the United States and Canada, have their own ambulance service.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="District">District</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: District">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regional_hospital" title="Regional hospital">Regional hospital</a></div>
<p>A district hospital typically is the major health care facility in its region, with large numbers of beds for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intensive_care" title="Intensive care">intensive care</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critical_care_medicine" title="Critical care medicine">critical care</a>, and long-term care.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, "district hospital" refers specifically to a class of healthcare facility created shortly after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> to address a shortage of hospital beds in many local communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLF2013_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-DHLF2013-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knox2013_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Knox2013-8">[8]</a></sup> Even today, district hospitals are the sole public hospitals in 19 of California's counties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLF2013_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-DHLF2013-7">[7]</a></sup> and are the sole locally-accessible hospital within nine additional counties in which one or more other hospitals are present at a substantial distance from a local community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLF2013_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-DHLF2013-7">[7]</a></sup> Twenty-eight of California's rural hospitals and 20 of its critical-access hospitals are district hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knox2013_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Knox2013-8">[8]</a></sup> They are formed by local municipalities, have boards that are individually elected by their local communities, and exist to serve local needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLF2013_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-DHLF2013-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knox2013_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Knox2013-8">[8]</a></sup> They are a particularly important provider of healthcare to uninsured patients and patients with <a href="/wiki/Medi-Cal" title="Medi-Cal">Medi-Cal</a> (which is California's <a href="/wiki/Medicaid" title="Medicaid">Medicaid</a> program, serving low-income persons, some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senior_citizens" title="Senior citizens">senior citizens</a>, persons with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disabilities" title="Disabilities">disabilities</a>, children in <a href="/wiki/Foster_care" title="Foster care">foster care</a>, and pregnant women).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLF2013_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-DHLF2013-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knox2013_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Knox2013-8">[8]</a></sup> In 2012, district hospitals provided $54 million in uncompensated care in California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knox2013_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-Knox2013-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialized">Specialized</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Specialized">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg/170px-Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg/255px-Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg/340px-Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Starship_Children%27s_Health_Auckland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starship_Children%27s_Health" title="Starship Children's Health">Starship Children's Health</a> is a children's hospital in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>, New Zealand</div></div></div>
<p>A specialty hospital is primarily and exclusively dedicated to one or a few related <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">medical specialties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Subtypes include <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_hospital" title="Rehabilitation hospital">rehabilitation hospitals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_hospital" title="Children's hospital">children's hospitals</a>, seniors' (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geriatric" title="Geriatric">geriatric</a>) hospitals, <a href="/wiki/Long-term_acute_care_facility" title="Long-term acute care facility">long-term acute care facilities</a>, and hospitals for dealing with specific medical needs such as <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">psychiatric</a> problems (see <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric hospital</a>), <a href="/wiki/List_of_cancer_hospitals" title="List of cancer hospitals">cancer treatment</a>, certain disease categories such as cardiac, oncology, or orthopedic problems, and so forth.
</p><p>In Germany specialised hospitals are called <i>Fachkrankenhaus</i>; an example is <a href="/wiki/Fachkrankenhaus_Coswig" title="Fachkrankenhaus Coswig">Fachkrankenhaus Coswig</a> (thoracic surgery). In India, specialty hospitals are known as <i>super-specialty hospitals</i> and are distinguished from multispecialty hospitals which are composed of several specialties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Specialised hospitals can help reduce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_costs" title="Health care costs">health care costs</a> compared to general hospitals. For example, <a href="/wiki/Narayana_Health" title="Narayana Health">Narayana Health's</a> cardiac unit in <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> specialises in cardiac surgery and allows for a significantly greater number of patients. It has 3,000 beds and performs 3,000 in paediatric cardiac operations annually, the largest number in the world for such a facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fastcompany_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-fastcompany-11">[11]</a></sup> Surgeons are paid on a fixed salary instead of per operation, thus when the number of procedures increases, the hospital is able to take advantage of <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a> and reduce its cost per procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fastcompany_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-fastcompany-11">[11]</a></sup> Each specialist may also become more efficient by working on one procedure like a <a href="/wiki/Production_line" title="Production line">production line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching">Teaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Teaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">Teaching hospital</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2589" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg/220px-Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg/330px-Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg/440px-Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial-Picture-of-Jackson-e1445995779731.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jackson_Memorial_Hospital" title="Jackson Memorial Hospital">Jackson Memorial Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Health_District_(Miami)" title="Health District (Miami)">Miami's Health District</a>, the primary teaching hospital for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">University of Miami</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Leonard_M._Miller_School_of_Medicine" title="Leonard M. Miller School of Medicine">Leonard M. Miller School of Medicine</a> and the largest hospital in the United States with 1,547 beds<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McMasterUMedical.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/220px-McMasterUMedical.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/330px-McMasterUMedical.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/440px-McMasterUMedical.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McMasterUMedical.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/McMaster_University_Medical_Centre" title="McMaster University Medical Centre">McMaster University Medical Centre</a> is a teaching hospital in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton, Ontario</a></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospital</a> delivers healthcare to patients as well as training to prospective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Professionals" title="Medical Professionals">medical professionals</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_students" title="Medical students">medical students</a> and student <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nurses</a>. It may be linked to a <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_school" title="Nursing school">nursing school</a>, and may be involved in <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">medical research</a>. Students may also observe clinical work in the hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinics">Clinics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Clinics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinics" title="Clinics">Clinics</a> generally provide only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outpatient" title="Outpatient">outpatient</a> services, but some may have a few inpatient beds and a limited range of services that may otherwise be found in typical hospitals.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Departments_or_wards">Departments or wards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Departments or wards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1799" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png/350px-Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png/525px-Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png/700px-Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospital-beds-per-1000-people.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hospital beds per 1000 people 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg/300px-Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg/450px-Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg/600px-Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_beds_in_OECD.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hospital beds per inhabitants</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg/220px-ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg/330px-ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg/440px-ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ER_room_after_a_trauma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Resuscitation" title="Resuscitation">Resuscitation</a> room bed after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_trauma" title="Physical trauma">trauma</a> intervention, showing the highly technical equipment of modern hospitals</div></div></div>
<p>A hospital contains one or more wards that house <a href="/wiki/Hospital_bed" title="Hospital bed">hospital beds</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inpatient" title="Inpatient">inpatients</a>. It may also have acute services such as an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">emergency department</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operating_theatre" title="Operating theatre">operating theatre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intensive_care_unit" title="Intensive care unit">intensive care unit</a>, as well as a range of <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">medical specialty</a> departments. A well-equipped hospital may be classified as a <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">trauma center</a>. They may also have other services such as a <a href="/wiki/Hospital_pharmacy" title="Hospital pharmacy">hospital pharmacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiology" title="Radiology">radiology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pathology" title="Pathology">pathology</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_laboratories" title="Medical laboratories">medical laboratories</a>. Some hospitals have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outpatient" title="Outpatient">outpatient departments</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Behavioral_health" title="Behavioral health">behavioral health</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">dentistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Physical_medicine_and_rehabilitation" title="Physical medicine and rehabilitation">rehabilitation services</a>.
</p><p>A hospital may also have a <a href="/wiki/Nursing_management" title="Nursing management">department of nursing</a>, headed by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_nursing_officer" title="Chief nursing officer">chief nursing officer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nursing_management#Director_of_nursing" title="Nursing management">director of nursing</a>. This department is responsible for the administration of professional nursing practice, <a href="/wiki/Nursing_research" title="Nursing research">research</a>, and policy for the hospital.
</p><p>Many units have both a nursing and a medical director that serve as administrators for their respective disciplines within that unit. For example, within an intensive care nursery, a medical director is responsible for physicians and medical care, while the nursing manager is responsible for all the nurses and nursing care.
</p><p>Support units may include a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_records_department" title="Medical records department">medical records department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Release_of_information_department" title="Release of information department">release of information department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Technical_support" title="Technical support">technical support</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clinical_engineering" title="Clinical engineering">clinical engineering</a>, facilities management, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_operations" title="Plant operations">plant operations</a>, dining services, and security departments.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remote_monitoring">Remote monitoring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Remote monitoring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> stimulated the development of virtual wards across the British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHS" title="NHS">NHS</a>.  Patients are  managed at home, monitoring their own oxygen levels using an oxygen saturation probe if necessary and supported by telephone.  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Hertfordshire_Hospitals_NHS_Trust" title="West Hertfordshire Hospitals NHS Trust">West Hertfordshire Hospitals NHS Trust</a> managed around 1200 patients at home between March and June 2020 and planned to continue the system after COVID-19, initially for respiratory patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mersey_Care_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Mersey Care NHS Foundation Trust">Mersey Care NHS Foundation Trust</a> started a COVID Oximetry@Home service in April 2020.  This enables them to monitor more than 5000  patients a day in their own homes.  The technology allows nurses, carers, or patients to record and monitor vital signs such as blood oxygen levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_hospitals" title="History of hospitals">History of hospitals</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_examples">Early examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Early examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptian_medicine" title="Ancient Egyptian medicine">Ancient Egyptian medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_medicine" title="Ancient Greek medicine">Ancient Greek medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine_in_ancient_Rome" title="Medicine in ancient Rome">Medicine in ancient Rome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Medical_community_of_ancient_Rome" title="Medical community of ancient Rome">Medical community of ancient Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kos_Asklepeion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="876" data-file-width="1453" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kos_Asklepeion.jpg/220px-Kos_Asklepeion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kos_Asklepeion.jpg/330px-Kos_Asklepeion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kos_Asklepeion.jpg/440px-Kos_Asklepeion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kos_Asklepeion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the <i>Askleipion</i> of <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a>, the best preserved instance of an Asklepieion.</div></div></div>
<p>In early India, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fa_Xian" title="Fa Xian">Fa Xian</a>, a Chinese Buddhist monk who travelled across India c. AD 400, recorded examples of healing institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> According to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahavamsa" title="Mahavamsa">Mahavamsa</a></i>, the ancient chronicle of Sinhalese royalty, written in the sixth century AD, King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pandukabhaya_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Pandukabhaya of Sri Lanka">Pandukabhaya of Sri Lanka</a> (r. 437–367 BC) had lying-in-homes and hospitals (Sivikasotthi-Sala).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_of_Guneshapur" title="Academy of Guneshapur">hospital and medical training centre</a> also existed at <a href="/wiki/Gundeshapur" title="Gundeshapur">Gundeshapur</a>, a major city in southwest of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persian_Empire" title="Sassanid Persian Empire">Sassanid Persian Empire</a> founded in AD 271 by <a href="/wiki/Shapur_I" title="Shapur I">Shapur I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>, temples dedicated to the healer-god <a href="/wiki/Asclepius" title="Asclepius">Asclepius</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Asclepeion" title="Asclepeion">Asclepeion</a> functioned as centres of medical advice, prognosis, and healing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The Asclepeia spread to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. While public healthcare was non-existent in the Roman Empire, military hospitals called <i>valetudinaria</i> did exist stationed in military barracks and would serve the soldiers and slaves within the fort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ziegler_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ziegler-21">[21]</a></sup> Evidence exists that some civilian hospitals, while unavailable to the Roman population, were occasionally privately built in extremely wealthy Roman households located in the countryside for that family, although this practice seems to have ended in 80 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1722" data-file-width="2364" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg/220px-Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg/330px-Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg/440px-Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lankan_Traditional_Medicine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruins of a two thousand-year-old hospital were discovered in the historical city of <a href="/wiki/Anuradhapura" title="Anuradhapura">Anuradhapura</a> <a href="/wiki/Mihintale" title="Mihintale">Mihintale</a> <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_medicine" title="Byzantine medicine">Byzantine medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medieval_medicine_of_Western_Europe" title="Medieval medicine of Western Europe">Medieval medicine of Western Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Medicine_in_the_medieval_Islamic_world" title="Medicine in the medieval Islamic world">Medicine in the medieval Islamic world</a></div><p>The declaration of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as an accepted religion in the Roman Empire drove an expansion of the provision of care. Following the <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea" title="First Council of Nicaea">First Council of Nicaea</a> in AD 325 construction of a hospital in every <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedral</a> town was begun, including among the earliest hospitals by <a href="/wiki/Sampson_the_Hospitable" title="Sampson the Hospitable">Saint Sampson</a> in <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> and by <a href="/wiki/Basil_of_Caesarea" title="Basil of Caesarea">Basil, bishop of Caesarea</a> in modern-day Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> By the twelfth century, Constantinople had two well-organised hospitals, staffed by doctors who were both male and female. Facilities included systematic treatment procedures and specialised wards for various diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_(1878)_-_TIMEA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="827" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg/220px-Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg/330px-Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg/440px-Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Door_of_the_Moristan_of_Kala%27oon_(1878)_-_TIMEA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Qalawun_complex" title="Qalawun complex">Qalawun complex</a> in Cairo, Egypt which housed the notable Mansuri hospital.</div></div></div>
<p>The earliest general hospital in the Islamic world was built in 805 in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harun_Al-Rashid" title="Harun Al-Rashid">Harun Al-Rashid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glubb_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glubb-26">[26]</a></sup> By the 10th century, Baghdad had five more hospitals, while <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a> had six hospitals by the 15th century, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">Córdoba</a> alone had 50 major hospitals<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2020)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, many exclusively for the military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aramco0317_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-aramco0317-27">[27]</a></sup> The Islamic <i><a href="/wiki/Bimaristan" title="Bimaristan">bimaristan</a></i> served as a center of medical treatment, as well <a href="/wiki/Nursing_home" title="Nursing home">nursing home</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lunatic_asylum" title="Lunatic asylum">lunatic asylum</a>. It typically treated the poor, as the rich would have been treated in their own homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nlm_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-nlm-28">[28]</a></sup> Hospitals in this era were the first to require medical diplomas to license doctors, and compensation for negligence could be made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alatas_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alatas-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Hospitals were forbidden by law to turn away patients who were unable to pay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdouglas_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-sdouglas-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (September 2019)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> These hospitals were financially supported by <a href="/wiki/Waqf" title="Waqf">waqfs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdouglas_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-sdouglas-30">[30]</a></sup> as well as state funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aramco0317_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-aramco0317-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_and_Enlightenment_Europe">Early modern and Enlightenment Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Early modern and Enlightenment Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ancien-Hopital.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1520" data-file-width="1902" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ancien-Hopital.jpg/220px-Ancien-Hopital.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ancien-Hopital.jpg/330px-Ancien-Hopital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ancien-Hopital.jpg/440px-Ancien-Hopital.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ancien-Hopital.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hospital ward in sixteenth century France.</div></div></div>
<p>In Europe the medieval concept of Christian care evolved during the sixteenth and seventeenth centuries into a secular one. In England, after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_monasteries" title="Dissolution of the monasteries">dissolution of the monasteries</a> in 1540 by King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>, the church abruptly ceased to be the supporter of hospitals, and only by direct petition from the citizens of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, were the hospitals <a href="/wiki/St_Bartholomew%27s_Hospital" title="St Bartholomew's Hospital">St Bartholomew's</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Thomas%27s_Hospital" title="St Thomas's Hospital">St Thomas's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bethlem_Royal_Hospital" title="Bethlem Royal Hospital">St Mary of Bethlehem's</a> (Bedlam) endowed directly by the crown; this was the first instance of secular support being provided for medical institutions.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1852" data-file-width="2660" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg/220px-Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg/330px-Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg/440px-Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guy%27s_Hospital00.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1820 Engraving of <a href="/wiki/Guy%27s_Hospital" title="Guy's Hospital">Guy's Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> one of the first voluntary hospitals to be established in 1724</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg/220px-Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg/330px-Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg/440px-Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ruinas_San_Nicolas_de_Bari_CCSD_09_2018_1414.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruins of the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_San_Nicol%C3%A1s_de_Bari" title="Hospital San Nicolás de Bari">Hospital San Nicolás de Bari</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, recognized by UNESCO for being the oldest hospital built in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Built between 1514 and 1541.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pennsylvania_Hospital_(Highsmith).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3432" data-file-width="4332" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png/220px-Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png/330px-Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png/440px-Pennsylvania_Hospital_%28Highsmith%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pennsylvania_Hospital_(Highsmith).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Hospital" title="Pennsylvania Hospital">Pennsylvania Hospital</a> (now part of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_Health_System" title="University of Pennsylvania Health System">University of Pennsylvania Health System</a>). Founded in 1751, it is the earliest established public hospital in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericasFirstHospital_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmericasFirstHospital-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrhp_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrhp-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[a]</a></sup> It is also home to America's first surgical amphitheatre and its first medical library.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_hospital" title="Voluntary hospital">voluntary hospital</a> movement began in the early 18th century, with hospitals being founded in London by the 1720s, including <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Hospital" title="Westminster Hospital">Westminster Hospital</a> (1719) promoted by the <a href="/wiki/Private_bank" title="Private bank">private bank</a> <a href="/wiki/C._Hoare_%26_Co" title="C. Hoare &amp; Co">C. Hoare &amp; Co</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guy%27s_Hospital" title="Guy's Hospital">Guy's Hospital</a> (1724) funded from the bequest of the wealthy merchant, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Guy" title="Thomas Guy">Thomas Guy</a>.
</p><p>Other hospitals sprang up in London and other British cities over the century, many paid for by private subscriptions. St Bartholomew's in London was rebuilt from 1730 to 1759,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> and the London Hospital, Whitechapel, opened in 1752.
</p><p>These hospitals represented a turning point in the function of the institution; they began to evolve from being basic places of care for the sick to becoming centres of medical innovation and discovery and the principal place for the <a href="/wiki/Medical_education" title="Medical education">education</a> and training of prospective practitioners. Some of the era's greatest <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeons</a> and doctors worked and passed on their knowledge at the hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> They also changed from being mere homes of refuge to being complex institutions for the provision of medicine and care for sick. The <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charité">Charité</a> was founded in Berlin in 1710 by King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Frederick I of Prussia</a> as a response to an outbreak of plague.
</p><p>The concept of voluntary hospitals also spread to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_America" title="Colonial America">Colonial America</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Hospital" title="Bellevue Hospital">Bellevue Hospital</a> opened in 1736 (as a workhouse, then later becoming a hospital); the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Hospital" title="Pennsylvania Hospital">Pennsylvania Hospital</a> opened in 1752, <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_Center" title="Weill Cornell Medical Center">New York Hospital</a> (now Weill Cornell Medical Center)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> in 1771, and <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Hospital" title="Massachusetts General Hospital">Massachusetts General Hospital</a> in 1811.
</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_General_Hospital" title="Vienna General Hospital">Vienna General Hospital</a> opened in 1784 (instantly becoming the world's largest hospital), physicians acquired a new facility that gradually developed into one of the most important research centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> era charitable innovation was the dispensary; these would issue the poor with <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicines</a> free of charge. The London Dispensary opened its doors in 1696 as the first such clinic in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. The idea was slow to catch on until the 1770s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> when many such organisations began to appear, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Dispensary_of_Edinburgh" title="Public Dispensary of Edinburgh">Public Dispensary of Edinburgh</a> (1776), the Metropolitan Dispensary and Charitable Fund (1779) and the <a href="/wiki/Finsbury_Dispensary" title="Finsbury Dispensary">Finsbury Dispensary</a> (1780). Dispensaries were also opened in New York 1771, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> 1786, and Boston 1796.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Hospital,_Stonehouse" title="Royal Naval Hospital, Stonehouse">Royal Naval Hospital, Stonehouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, was a pioneer of hospital design in having "pavilions" to minimize the spread of infection. <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a> visited in 1785, and commented "I never saw anything of the kind so complete; every part is so convenient, and so admirably neat. But there is nothing superfluous, and nothing purely ornamented, either within or without." This revolutionary design was made more widely known by <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a>, the philanthropist. In 1787 the French government sent two scholar administrators, <a href="/wiki/Charles-Augustin_de_Coulomb" title="Charles-Augustin de Coulomb">Coulomb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Ren%C3%A9_Tenon" title="Jacques-René Tenon">Tenon</a>, who had visited most of the hospitals in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> They were impressed and the "pavilion" design was copied in France and throughout Europe.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration,_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2609" data-file-width="3970" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg/220px-%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg/330px-%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg/440px-%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration%2C_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27One_of_the_wards_in_the_hospital_at_Scutari%27._Wellcome_M0007724_-_restoration,_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A ward of the hospital at <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Csk%C3%BCdar" title="Üsküdar">Scutari</a> where <a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a> worked and helped to restructure the modern hospital</div></div></div>
<p>English physician <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Percival" title="Thomas Percival">Thomas Percival</a> (1740–1804) wrote a comprehensive system of medical conduct, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Ethics;_or,_a_Code_of_Institutes_and_Precepts,_Adapted_to_the_Professional_Conduct_of_Physicians_and_Surgeons" title="Medical Ethics; or, a Code of Institutes and Precepts, Adapted to the Professional Conduct of Physicians and Surgeons">Medical Ethics; or, a Code of Institutes and Precepts, Adapted to the Professional Conduct of Physicians and Surgeons</a></i> (1803) that set the standard for many textbooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> In the mid-19th century, hospitals and the medical profession became more professionalised, with a reorganisation of hospital management along more bureaucratic and administrative lines. The <a href="/wiki/Apothecaries_Act_1815" title="Apothecaries Act 1815">Apothecaries Act 1815</a> made it compulsory for medical students to practise for at least half a year at a hospital as part of their training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a> pioneered the modern profession of <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> when she set an example of compassion, commitment to patient care and diligent and thoughtful hospital administration. The first official nurses' training programme, the Nightingale School for Nurses, was opened in 1860, with the mission of training nurses to work in hospitals, to work with the poor and to teach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Nightingale was instrumental in reforming the nature of the hospital, by improving <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> standards and changing the image of the hospital from a place the sick would go to die, to an institution devoted to recuperation and healing. She also emphasised the importance of <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistical measurement</a> for determining the success rate of a given intervention and pushed for <a href="/wiki/Public_administration" title="Public administration">administrative reform</a> at hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the late 19th century, the modern hospital was beginning to take shape with a proliferation of a variety of public and private hospital systems. By the 1870s, hospitals had more than trebled their original average intake of 3,000 patients. In continental Europe the new hospitals generally were built and run from public funds. The <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a>, the principal provider of health care in the United Kingdom, was founded in 1948. During the nineteenth century, the Second Viennese Medical School emerged with the contributions of physicians such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_Freiherr_von_Rokitansky" title="Carl Freiherr von Rokitansky">Carl Freiherr von Rokitansky</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josef_%C5%A0koda" title="Josef Škoda">Josef Škoda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Ritter_von_Hebra" title="Ferdinand Ritter von Hebra">Ferdinand Ritter von Hebra</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignaz_Philipp_Semmelweis" title="Ignaz Philipp Semmelweis">Ignaz Philipp Semmelweis</a>. Basic medical science expanded and specialisation advanced. Furthermore, the first dermatology, eye, as well as ear, nose, and throat clinics in the world were founded in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, being considered as the birth of specialised medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_and_beyond">20th century and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 20th century and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" and perspective in this section <b>deal primarily with the United States and do not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You may <a class="external text"
